< review>
I recently had a number of questions about 2020 tax planning and retirement planning.  I have an exceptionally knowledgeable tax expert at this H&R office, but she is on sabbatical doing continuing education and preparing for the 2020 tax season. Another experienced tax expert at this office, Sam, stepped up and offered to help me. I was much better able to lay out a good tax forecast for 2020 and apply the advise Sam gave me to regarding 401K withdrawal planning.  If you have tax planning issues, or are just looking for support with your tax filing, this office has genuine experts who have long-term experience and current tax law knowledge to help you.</review>

<user>111047325286429994771<//user>< Text>
I checked out both the dispensaries that were practically on the same block and decided to go with the Wellness Center vs. SureFyre Collective based on the fact that Wellness Center's prices were much more reasonable. I wasn't too impressed with SureFyre's smaller collection of flower choices (they have quite a few options with edibles/vapes/etc, but not much flower) and was pleasantly surprised to find out that the Wellness Center had much more flower options for different budgets. Matt helped me out and totally hooked it up- he was incredibly patient and helpful in his suggestions and worked within my budget and needs. He took the time to explain and suggest and his suggestions were right on. I walked out the door and when I looked in my bag found he had totally hooked it up and thrown in some goodies I wasn't expecting. If you're looking for good quality flower and Matt is around, he's your man. I am not into the hype of marijuana, so if you want down to earth people and reasonable prices, check out the Wellness Center. I ended up trying the Ingrid Indica and its one of the best buds I've ever had! Thanks again, Matt!<//Text>

What a stunning way to explore Griffith Park and see the beautiful city of LA in ways I couldn't possibly have imagined. Our guide, Elizabeth, was incredible! <userid>117870333184419940614<//userid>< review>
So much fun!!! I have done a number of bike tours in various cities around the world and this was the most entertaining! The guides were fantastic. Chatty, engaging, friendly! What more could you ask??

The tour itself was awesome, we saw so much of LA and learnt so much random trivia along the way.

There are definitely some hills (Beverly Hills isn't just a pretty name!) and you cover a lot of ground so be prepared for a sore butt if you are like me and don't ride in your day to day life. So worth it though!

The team provide water and snacks and lunch was available for purchase at Venice Beach. Perhaps most importantly, an ice cold beer was also provided back at the depot at the end of the tour.

What more can I say? Do this tour!! You wont regret it!</review>

<review>This was my first trip to the States and therefore the first time in LA. I only had 3 days passing through, so immediately booked a guided bike tour around the city, thinking this would be the best way to avoid traffic, see all the sights and get a little exercise done!

I was certainly not disappointed! Despite an unusual downpour, our guide, Erik, kept our small group of three in high spirits with stories from his youth growing up in the area and explaining about the awesome mix of cultures in the city. His breadth and depth of knowledge on all things LA-related is astounding! From pointing out little-known architectural gems to knowing the history of ownership of particular houses and estates, going all the way back to the previous century, there was no question he couldn't answer. By the time we were at the coast in the afternoon, it was sunny and warming up, leading to a great cruise along the coast and back to West Hollywood just as the sun was setting.

If you have a day, are in reasonable shape and want a unique way to experience around 30 miles of the city, this is definitely something you should try! I'll be back in LA in a few months' time and I've already promised the crew at Bikes and Hikes LA that I'll be back to experience this epic tour again - hopefully with a little less rain!</review>< Pics>
None< /Pics>

< review>
06/23/19 We went on the LA in a day tour and it was excellent. We covered so many areas in just one day. It was amazing how many places we can say we have been and seen after this tour. Our tour guide, George was terrific! He shared a lot of information about the area. Our epic adventure was especially challenging and George took care of everything. I would highly recommend any of their tours. This was a very physically challenging ride. The first few hours are hilly. It is also over 30 miles. My first tip would be unless you cycle 20+ miles 3X per week, upgrade to an E-bike. They are very easy to use and well worth the extra fee. This way you have the option of having assistance with the hills if needed. Also, consider what terrain you are accustomed to; we came from Florida where it is relatively flat, so this was especially difficult. Another tip, if you leave your purse or bag behind, make sure you take your sun screen out first. This was our favorite outing during our L.A. visit.  If you don't have this much time.  Consider one of their shorter tours.<//review>

< Text>
I was on the Sunset hike of Bikes and Hikes in Griffith Park. I had an absolute blast, our tour guide Kayla knew so much about the park itself, the city of Los Angeles, and she had a enthusiastic way of telling her stories that made it entertaining and easy to follow her. The hike itself is moderate, the first part is the "hardest", where we had to ascend about 400ft. It was well worth the view though. Fantastic outlooks over Los Angeles county and if you're lucky with the weather and it's not too hazy you get a nice view of the Hollywood sign. The tour was rounded off with visiting the Griffith observatory, where Kayla had a lot of interesting stories to tell again and we got to touch an age-old meteor piece. I definitely recommend taking a hike with Bikes and Hikes!</Text>

A. in a day bike tour! While we were on the go for four straight days this tour was hands down the best part of our whole trip! :)

The establishment was modern, clean and organized! We were pleasantly surprised when we found out that we were the only two who have booked the tour so we had the privilege of a private tour! We were greeted by a friendly employee the moment we arrived on the site. We were able to leave a bag of valuables at the site instead of urging it around all day. We were given a quick safety review and quick introductions were made then we were on our way!

Our guide was Daniel and he was training Chase the day of our tour! Daniel was able to provide insightful anecdotes all along our excursion. He was able to answer all of our questions about the sites and sounds of L. A. He encouraed us to wonder, told us stories, peeked our curiosity, pointed out the various city boundaries and landmarks, made us laugh and best of all made us feel like we were already long time friends. Daniel not only navigated us through the busy streets but also helped us feel safe in uncharted territory.

The pace of our tour was perfect. We took several breaks for restrooms and water. We stopped and had a delicious lunch by the beach. Which was wisely pre- arranged in the morning so we didn't have to wait in any lines for our food.

We were provided with safety vests and well fitted helmets, water bottles and well maintained bicycles. We loved every minute and would recommend this tour to anyone who likes biking, exploring and hearing about the ins and outs of the area!

Thank you Bikes and Hikes for setting up this awesome Tour!<//text>

Every time I am in LA I book a tour with Bikes and Hikes and everytime I am glad I did. Earlier this month we did the LA in a day bike tour again. Jason Hill< /user_name>
<Pics>None< /Pics><response>{'time': 1472679255063, 'text': 'Hi Jason!\nThank you for writing this awesome review. We highly appreciate and enjoyed reading it!\nWe are very happy to hear that you had a blast on your hike.\nWe would love to see you again, perhaps on one of our biking tours!'}</response>< text>
"Hi Mom!  I made it to the top of Hollywood!"

Yes, I sent that ridiculous text, accompanied with a goofy tourist smile and my fist pumped up in the air.  The backdrop?  A breathtaking view of the mountains, the gorgeous skyline, and the entirety of Los Angeles.

Believe it or not, I live here.  But to my delight, the Bikes and Hikes Sunset Tour reignited my love affair with with LA!  It allowed me to experience my city through a new lens - a lens that my mind (and my camera roll) will never forget.

Leading my hike was a handsome tour guide by the name of Solomon.  He had an adorable Colombian accent and a killer sense of humor.  OH!  And speaking of killers - did you know that Colonel Griffith shot his wife in the head?  She survived the assassination attempt and got a well-deserved divorce. You'll learn allll the details of this crazytown story and waaay way more during your hike!  Somehow, Solomon will manage to give you a great workout, show you spectacular views, and shock you with an intricate history of Griffith Park & Hollywood!

OK... now let's get down to the nitty gritty.  If you're like me, you like to rock your cuteness wherever you go.  You'll probably wear your cute shorts with a cute top and hope to scope out the cute celebs that may be around now that Runyon is closed.  Just make sure that your cute sneakers have a good grip, because we definitely HIKE!

Oooh.  One more word of advice!  Bring a camera!  If you're a tourist and you walk around with a gigantic tourist camera - I'm all "hashtag yaaaaaaaas" for you right now!  It is SO worth it.  The pictures you'll take will blow your mind.  Once you get to the top of the Mount Hollywood Trail, you may even tear up a bit - it's kind of impossible to believe that something so beautiful exists until you see it in person.  If you don't have a fancy schmancy camera - it's all good.  Just be sure to juice up your cell phone battery before the hike - you'll want to put that smartphone camera to #werq!

There's so much more I could tell you, but I can't cheat you out of experiencing this on your own.  You'll get to see mind-blowing views of nature in its purest form, have an impromptu history lesson, see the filming locations of some of your favorite movies (spoiler alert: Charlie's Angels!!), AND burn off all the delicious Mexican food you've been eating!  The San Gabriel Mountains, The Hollywood Sign, the Los Angeles Skyline and a Tighter Waist Line now all have something in common: they're all fabulous perks of Bikes and Hikes LA!</text>

< text>
CASH ONLY but they are fast, tasty, and a great value. I wish they were open on Sundays! Would be â­â­â­â­â­ if they had longer hours and were open on Sundays.

Typical tacqueria style value super tacos & super burritos with your choice of meat. Personally, I like their chicken, but the pork & carne asada are good too. FYI: Hot sauce/salsa is kept in squease bottles in the fridge (along with a selection of Mexican sodas). The red salsa is spicier than the salsa verde. They also use only corn tortillas for the tacos, which makes them a good gluten-free option.

Located in that ancient run-down parking lot on Bascom still bearing the name "Dick's Center." They're easy to overlook. Due to their location on the corner of the strip, the glare from the sun can be quite daunting at certain times of day, but many customers seem to grab food to-go, as there are only a few tables indoors and a few tables outdoors anyway.< /text>

<user>102288761280391594138< /user><user_name>Sashwat Singh< /user_name>< Date>
1527721173610</Date>
< Rate>
5< /Rate>
< text>
I'm the kind of person who will NEVER order Tacos when I'm out to eat Mexican food. Chimichangas, Burritos, Fajitas, Tortas, Tostadas, Flautas... literally anything sounds better to me than a Taco. And I've tried every item on the Tacos Mexicos menu.

The verdict: Get the tacos. They are so much better than any other item on the menu and the best value at $3 (veggie super tacos are $2.70). They jam pack the super tacos with filling (a high ratio of meat). The cheese is melted in between the tortillas. Make sure you ask to get them extra crispy for a crunchy outside and soft inside you won't be able to resist. My particular favorite is the BBQ Pork. Haven't stomached the beef tongue or pork cheeks (those just sound too weird to me) and haven't tried the chile relleno, but I'd say the BBQ pork is better than everything else (chicken, carnitas, carne asada).

Trust me -- I know you like burritos and tortas, but I've been in that same predicament... I've gotten those just to try something new and every time have immediately regretted not just getting two super tacos for nearly the same price. There's a reason it's called Tacos Mexicos. Get the tacos.< /text>

<response>None</response>< date>
1603776986803<//date>
<username>Catherine A. Montgomery< /username>< Review>
Centrally located, Aloha Steakhouse is the ONLY beach restaurant. It has a Hawaiian influence, serving variety of entrees such as chicken, steak, seafood and fish. The menu features an array of contemporary lunch and dinner favorites, plus Island specialties and decadent desserts.

At time of visit, they offered patio dining only, reservation recommended as seating on patio is limited. Tables were 6 feet apart, but despite the distance, local patrons of this place were very friendly. Also at time of visit, fencing was placed around the patio area. There is a spacious, full-service bar (you may order but can not drink inside) offering a wide variety of craft cocktails, martinis and beer.

Our server was very friendly. Because the menu was extensive, she was happy to make suggestions based on our taste that evening. We chose Teriyaki Chicken Kabob on bed of rice and Seared Scallops with spinach and cream sauce, which we paired with Chandon split and Mai Tai (a little strong but it hit the spot!). The chicken and scallops were quite tender, scallops fresh and seasoned well.

We were little full by end of our meal, but curious about desserts. We decided to pass, but our server was kind enough to comp a house favorite, Kona Pie - Macadamia nuts, ice cream on Oreo cookie, topped with bittersweet chocolate syrup and whipped cream. It was quite rich, but we enjoyed every bite, saving a few bites for later that evening.

There was a fantastic casual vibe here, and the food was fantastic. We will visit this restaurant again the next time we are in the area.</Review>

< review>
Arrived for dinner on a Sunday.  Had a hankering for steak.  Choose this place from the few places I quickly scanned.  You need to use the public parking garage adjacent to the restaurant but the restaurant will validate your parking ticket.  Was deciding between the ribeye or filet mignon.  Decided to try the ribeye thinking that it has to be good, given this is a steak place.  Had a choice of three salads, decided on something called the wedge which was iceberg lettuce with blue cheese dressing, bacon bits, tomatoes and maybe something else - very good.  Then the steak with steamed vegetables.  The veggies - good.  The steak - very disappointing; too thin, not a good cut and too salty.  Needed A1 with it.  Saw something on the desert menu I wanted to try for desert - kono ice cream pie with slivers of nuts on top - very good; by far the best part of the meal.  My search for a good steak goes on.  This place will stay in business because of the sides and deserts but in my opinion, the steaks are lacking here.</review>

< Text>
Arrived for dinner on a Sunday.  Had a hankering for steak.  Choose this place from the few places I quickly scanned.  You need to use the public parking garage adjacent to the restaurant but the restaurant will validate your parking ticket.  Was deciding between the ribeye or filet mignon.  Decided to try the ribeye thinking that it has to be good, given this is a steak place.  Had a choice of three salads, decided on something called the wedge which was iceberg lettuce with blue cheese dressing, bacon bits, tomatoes and maybe something else - very good.  Then the steak with steamed vegetables.  The veggies - good.  The steak - very disappointing; too thin, not a good cut and too salty.  Needed A1 with it.  Saw something on the desert menu I wanted to try for desert - kono ice cream pie with slivers of nuts on top - very good; by far the best part of the meal.  My search for a good steak goes on.  This place will stay in business because of the sides and deserts but in my opinion, the steaks are lacking here.</Text>

<review>I wouldn't classify this establishment as a "steakhouse".
Service was extremely slow and subpar. When looking at the menu all the steaks came with some strange heavy smothering sauce to mask the extremely poor quality of the meat. On top of the weird sauce and poor meat, with sitting outside they refused to attempt their signature flambeau table side service even with the patio being protected with clear tall glass barrier. Speaking of the patio, it lies next to the main walkway for the public to stop and stare at you as if you were a caged lion with the look of defeat in your eyes. With the massive barrier surrounding the patio it made the environment stale and stuffy, negating the beautiful ocean breeze and sounds.
As we left a very stiff, stuffy, stale, half eaten dinner at the supposed "steakhouse" a woman, smoking just past the doors of the "steakhouse" asked of we enjoyed our dinner with great enthusiasm and hope. Our response was "if you're waiting to eat there don't..." as we explained our disappointing dinner. She quickly changed her enthusiasm to dismay, "well, we didn't expect such a large crowd tonight."  Which led me to believe she was apart of the "steakhouse". As if being crowded, isn't that what you want as a business, is an excuse for the lackluster performance by the "steakhouse".
With all this being said, the ONLY reason we had dinner at this "steakhouse" is because we had a gift card. If I were to get another gift card or offered a free meal at this "steakhouse" I would not return.
